</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Smart_city" title="Smart city">Smart city</a></div>
<p>The development of smart cities has seen the increased adoption of surveillance technologies by governments, although the primary purpose of surveillance in such cities is to <a href="/wiki/Smart_city#Characteristics" title="Smart city">use information and communication technologies</a> to improve the urban environment. The implementation of such technology by <a href="/wiki/Smart_city#Flagship_cases" title="Smart city">a number of cities</a> has resulted in increased efficiencies in urban infrastructure as well as improved community participation.</p>
<p>The development of smart city technology has also led to increased potential for unwarranted <a href="/wiki/Surveillance_issues_in_smart_cities#Privacy_and_autonomy" title="Surveillance issues in smart cities">intrusions into privacy and restrictions upon autonomy</a>. The widespread incorporation of information and communication technologies within the daily life of urban residents results in increases in the <a href="/wiki/Surveillance_issues_in_smart_cities#Panopticism" title="Surveillance issues in smart cities">surveillance capacity of states</a> - to the extent that individuals may be unaware of what information is being accessed, when the access occurs and for what purpose. It is possible that such conditions could give rise to the <a href="/wiki/Surveillance_issues_in_smart_cities#Police_state" title="Surveillance issues in smart cities">development of an electronic police state</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Electronic_police_state">Electronic police state</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mass_surveillance&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Electronic police state">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_fear" title="Culture of fear">Culture of fear</a> and <a href="/wiki/Surveillance_issues_in_smart_cities" title="Surveillance issues in smart cities">Surveillance issues in smart cities</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Thai-coup-detat-2014-social-media-banner.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1971" data-file-width="2606" height="303" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Thai-coup-detat-2014-social-media-banner.jpg/400px-Thai-coup-detat-2014-social-media-banner.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Thai-coup-detat-2014-social-media-banner.jpg/600px-Thai-coup-detat-2014-social-media-banner.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Thai-coup-detat-2014-social-media-banner.jpg/800px-Thai-coup-detat-2014-social-media-banner.jpg 2x" width="400"/></a>

Banner in <a href="/wiki/Bangkok" title="Bangkok">Bangkok</a>, observed on the 30th of June 2014 during the <a href="/wiki/2014_Thai_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="2014 Thai coup d'état">2014 Thai coup d'état</a>, informing the <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thai</a> public that 'like' or 'share' activity on social media could land them in prison.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>An electronic <a href="/wiki/Police_state" title="Police state">police state</a> is a <a href="/wiki/State_(polity)" title="State (polity)">state</a> in which the government aggressively uses electronic technologies to record, collect, store, organize, analyze, search, and distribute information about its citizens.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPS-2008NationalRankings_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-EPS-2008NationalRankings-116">[116]</a></sup> Electronic police states also engage in mass government surveillance of <a href="/wiki/Landline" title="Landline">landline</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cellular_phone" title="Cellular phone">cellular</a> telephone traffic, mail, email, web surfing, Internet searches, radio, and other forms of electronic communication as well as widespread use of video surveillance. The information is usually collected in secret.</p>
<p>The crucial elements are not politically based, so long as the government can afford the technology and the populace will permit it to be used, an electronic police state can form. The continual use of electronic mass surveillance can result in constant low-level fear within the population, which can lead to <a href="/wiki/Self-censorship" title="Self-censorship">self-censorship</a> and exerts a powerful coercive force upon the populace.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Applications_of_Social_Control_Theory:_Criminality_and_Governmentality_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-Applications_of_Social_Control_Theory:_Criminality_and_Governmentality-117">[117]</a></sup></p>
<p>Seventeen factors for judging the development of an electronic police state were suggested in <i>The Electronic Police State: 2008 National Rankings</i>:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPS-2008NationalRankings_116-1"><a href="#cite_note-EPS-2008NationalRankings-116">[116]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><b>Daily documents</b>: Requirement for the use and tracking of state-issued <a href="/wiki/Identity_document" title="Identity document">identity documents</a> and registration.</li>
<li><b>Border and travel control</b>: Inspections at borders, searching computers and cell phones, demanding decryption of data, and tracking travel within as well as to and from a country.</li>
<li><b>Financial tracking</b>: A state’s ability to record and search <a href="/wiki/Financial_transaction" title="Financial transaction">financial transactions</a>: checks, credit cards, wires, etc.</li>
<li><b>Gag orders</b>: Restrictions on and criminal penalties for the disclosure of the existence of state surveillance programs.</li>
<li><b>Anti-crypto laws</b>: Outlawing or restricting <a href="/wiki/Cryptography" title="Cryptography">cryptography</a> and/or privacy enhancing technologies.</li>
<li><b>Lack of constitutional protections</b>: A lack of constitutional privacy protections or the routine overriding of such protections.</li>
<li><b>Data storage</b>: The ability of the state to store the data gathered.</li>
<li><b>Data search</b>: The ability to organize and search the data gathered.</li>
<li><b>Data retention requirements</b>: Laws that require Internet and other service providers to save detailed records of their customers’ Internet usage for a minimum period of time.
<ul>
<li><b>Telephone data retention requirements</b>: Laws that require telephone companies to record and save records of their customers’ telephone usage.</li>
<li><b>Cell phone data retention requirements</b>: Laws that require cellular telephone companies to record and save records of their customers’ usage and location.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><b>Medical records</b>: Government access to the records of medical service providers.</li>
<li><b>Enforcement</b>: The state’s ability to use force to seize anyone they want, whenever they want.</li>
<li><b>Lack of <i>habeas corpus</i></b>: Lack of a <a href="/wiki/Habeas_corpus" title="Habeas corpus">right for a person under arrest to be brought before a judge or into court</a> in a timely fashion or the overriding of such rights.</li>
<li><b>Lack of a police-intel barrier</b>: The lack of a barrier between police organizations and intelligence organizations, or the overriding of such barriers.</li>
<li><b>Covert hacking</b>: State operatives collecting, removing, or adding digital evidence to/from private computers without permission or the knowledge of the computers' owners.</li>
<li><b>Loose or no warrants</b>: Arrests or searches made without warrants or without careful examination and review of police statements and justifications by a truly independent judge or other third-party.</li>
</ul>
<p>The list includes factors that apply to other forms of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Police_State" title="Police State">police states</a>, such as the use of identity documents and police enforcement, but go considerably beyond them and emphasize the use of technology to gather and process the information collected.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_popular_culture">In popular culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mass_surveillance&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: In popular culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mass_surveillance_in_popular_culture" title="Mass surveillance in popular culture">Mass surveillance in popular culture</a></div>
<p>Mass surveillance has been prominently featured in a wide array of books, films, and other media. Perhaps the most iconic example of fictional mass surveillance is <a href="/wiki/George_Orwell" title="George Orwell">George Orwell</a>'s 1949 novel <i><a href="/wiki/Nineteen_Eighty-Four" title="Nineteen Eighty-Four">Nineteen Eighty-Four</a></i>, which depicts a <a href="/wiki/Dystopia" title="Dystopia">dystopian</a> surveillance state. Other media featuring mass surveillance systems include <i><a href="/wiki/Person_of_Interest_(TV_series)" title="Person of Interest (TV series)">Person of Interest</a></i> and other TV shows and other media types.</p>

<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em;">
<ul>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2013_global_surveillance_disclosures" title="2013 global surveillance disclosures">2013 global surveillance disclosures</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Broken_windows_theory" title="Broken windows theory">Broken windows theory</a>, a controversial theory that maintaining and monitoring urban environments in a well-ordered condition may stop further vandalism and escalation into more serious crime.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Closed-circuit_television" title="Closed-circuit television">Closed-circuit television</a> (CCTV)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Computer_and_network_surveillance" title="Computer and network surveillance">Computer and network surveillance</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Data_privacy" title="Data privacy">Data privacy</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Data_retention" title="Data retention">Data retention</a></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Discipline_and_Punish" title="Discipline and Punish">Discipline and Punish: The Birth of the Prison</a></i>, a 1975 book by the French philosopher <a href="/wiki/Michel_Foucault" title="Michel Foucault">Michel Foucault</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Global_surveillance" title="Global surveillance">Global surveillance</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Government_databases" title="Government databases">Government databases</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lawful_interception" title="Lawful interception">Lawful interception</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_government_surveillance_projects" title="List of government surveillance projects">List of government surveillance projects</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/National_security" title="National security">National security</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Network_theory" title="Network theory">Network analysis</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nothing_to_hide_argument" title="Nothing to hide argument">Nothing to hide argument</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pen_register" title="Pen register">Pen register</a>, originally an electronic device that records numbers (but not the audio) called from a particular telephone line, more recently any device or program that performs this function for electronic mail, other digital communications, and particularly communications over the Internet.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Phone_surveillance" title="Phone surveillance">Phone surveillance</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Police_state" title="Police state">Police state</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Radio-frequency_identification" title="Radio-frequency identification">Radio-frequency identification</a> (RFID), the wireless identification and tracking of tags attached to objects.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Right_to_privacy" title="Right to privacy">Right to privacy</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Security_culture" title="Security culture">Security culture</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Signals_intelligence" title="Signals intelligence">Signals intelligence</a> (SIGINT)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sousveillance" title="Sousveillance">Sousveillance</a>, the recording of an activity by a participant in the activity, cameras (or other sensors) affixed to property, or surveillance done by non-authorities.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Telephone_tapping_in_the_Eastern_Bloc" title="Telephone tapping in the Eastern Bloc">Telephone tapping in the Eastern Bloc</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tracking_system" title="Tracking system">Tracking system</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Traffic_analysis" title="Traffic analysis">Traffic analysis</a></li>
</ul>

BBC. 23 November 2014<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">6 December</span> 2014</span>. <q>Well I guess what he’s talking about is the fact that for certain aspects and certain of the more intrusive measures that our security service and police have available to them – i.e. Intercept, intercepting people’s telephones and some other intrusive measures – the decision is taken by the Secretary of State, predominantly me. A significant part of my job is looking at these warrants and signing these warrants. I think it’s ... Some people argue that should be to judges....I think it’s very important that actually those decisions are being taken by somebody who is democratically accountable to the public. I think that’s an important part of our system. I think it’s a strength of our system.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMass+surveillance&amp;rft.atitle=The+Andrew+Marr+Show+Interview%3A+Theresa+May%2C+MP+Home+Secretary&amp;rft.date=2014-11-23&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fnews.bbc.co.uk%2F1%2Fshared%2Fbsp%2Fhi%2Fpdfs%2F2311201402.pdf&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
